<p><i><b>Degrassi: The Next Generation</b></i> (later renamed <i><b>Degrassi</b></i> for seasons <a href="/wiki/Degrassi_(season_10)" title="Degrassi (season 10)">ten</a> through <a href="/wiki/Degrassi_(season_14)" title="Degrassi (season 14)">fourteen</a>) is a Canadian <a href="/wiki/Teen_drama" title="Teen drama">teen drama</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_series" title="Television series">television series</a> set in the <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi_(franchise)" title="Degrassi (franchise)">Degrassi</a></i> universe, which was created by <a href="/wiki/Linda_Schuyler" title="Linda Schuyler">Linda Schuyler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kit_Hood" title="Kit Hood">Kit Hood</a> in 1979. It is the fourth series in the <i>Degrassi</i> franchise, following <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kids_of_Degrassi_Street" title="The Kids of Degrassi Street">The Kids of Degrassi Street</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi_Junior_High" title="Degrassi Junior High">Degrassi Junior High</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi_High" title="Degrassi High">Degrassi High</a></i>. Like its predecessors, the series follows an <a href="/wiki/Ensemble_cast" title="Ensemble cast">ensemble cast</a> of students at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Degrassi_Community_School" title="Degrassi Community School">Degrassi Community School</a> who face various challenges often seen as taboo such as <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sex" title="Sex">sex</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen_pregnancy" title="Teen pregnancy">teen pregnancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullying</a>, <a href="/wiki/Date_rape" title="Date rape">date rape</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drug_abuse" title="Drug abuse">drug abuse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Body_image" title="Body image">self image</a>, <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-injury" title="Self-injury">self-injury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suicide" title="Suicide">suicide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">abortion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domestic_violence" title="Domestic violence">domestic violence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Death" title="Death">death</a>, <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racism</a> and many other issues.</p>
<p>The series was initially created by Linda Schuyler and <a href="/wiki/Yan_Moore" title="Yan Moore">Yan Moore</a>, and is produced by <a href="/wiki/Epitome_Pictures" title="Epitome Pictures">Epitome Pictures</a> (a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/DHX_Media" title="DHX Media">DHX Media</a>) in association with <a href="/wiki/Bell_Media" title="Bell Media">Bell Media</a>. The current executive producers are Schuyler, her husband <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stohn" title="Stephen Stohn">Stephen Stohn</a> and Brendon Yorke. The series is filmed at Epitome's studios in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, Ontario, rather than on the real <a href="/wiki/De_Grassi_Street" title="De Grassi Street">De Grassi Street</a> from which the franchise takes its name. <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> has been a critical success and has often received favourable reviews from <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, <i>The New York Times</i>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AfterElton.com" title="AfterElton.com">AfterElton.com</a>. In its initial years, it was frequently the most watched domestic drama series in Canada, and one of the highest-rated shows on <a href="/wiki/TeenNick" title="TeenNick">TeenNick</a> in the United States. In 2004, one episode received just under a million viewers in Canada, and over half a million viewers in the US. The series has won numerous awards, from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gemini_Award" title="Gemini Award">Geminis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_Canada" title="Writers Guild of Canada">Writers Guild of Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Directors_Guild_of_Canada" title="Directors Guild of Canada">Directors Guild of Canada</a>, and internationally from the <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Awards" title="Teen Choice Awards">Teen Choice Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Young_Artist_Award" title="Young Artist Award">Young Artist Awards</a>, and Prix Jeunesse.</p>
<p>The series premiered on <a href="/wiki/CTV_Television_Network" title="CTV Television Network">CTV</a> on October 14, 2001. During the ninth season in 2010, the series moved to <a href="/wiki/Much_(TV_channel)" title="Much (TV channel)">MuchMusic</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Degrassi_(season_10)" title="Degrassi (season 10)">tenth season</a> marked a change in production style, which saw the series become a <a href="/wiki/Telenovela" title="Telenovela">telenovela</a>, a daily <a href="/wiki/Soap_opera" title="Soap opera">soap opera</a>-style format, during the summer months, while the rest of the season aired during the standard fall-spring schedule on a weekly basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transgender_storyline_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-transgender_storyline-2">[2]</a></sup> The thirteenth season reverted to a weekly schedule and, part way through, moved to <a href="/wiki/MTV_(Canada)" title="MTV (Canada)">MTV Canada</a>. The series has been syndicated on cable television, and episodes are available on DVD and in <a href="/wiki/New_media" title="New media">new media</a> download formats from <a href="/wiki/Puretracks" title="Puretracks">Puretracks</a>, the <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Marketplace" title="Xbox Live Marketplace">Xbox Live Marketplace</a>. Internationally, <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> has been highly successful in the US, where it was broadcast on <a href="/wiki/TeenNick" title="TeenNick">TeenNick</a>, as well as being broadcast in 140 other countries.</p>
<p><i>The Next Generation</i> aired its final episode on August 2, 2015, after MTV Canada and TeenNick announced the show's cancellation. However, in 2016, the show, re-titled <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_Next_Class" title="Degrassi: Next Class">Degrassi: Next Class</a></i>, will move to <a href="/wiki/Family_Channel" title="Family Channel">Family Channel</a> in Canada and stream on <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a> in the United States as well as all other countries where the service is available (excluding Australia, France, and Canada until later 2016).</p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Impact"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Impact</span></a>
<ul>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Television_ratings"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Television ratings</span></a></li>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Critical_reception"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Critical reception</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concept">Concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mother_and_Child_Reunion_(Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation)#Production" title="Mother and Child Reunion (Degrassi: The Next Generation)">Production of pilot episode "Mother and Child Reunion"</a></div>
<p>The Degrassi universe was created in 1979 by Playing With Time, a production company owned by former school teacher Linda Schuyler and her partner Kit Hood. The franchise began with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Kids_of_Degrassi_Street" title="The Kids of Degrassi Street">The Kids of Degrassi Street</a></i>, which was spawned out of three half-hour short films. <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi_Junior_High" title="Degrassi Junior High">Degrassi Junior High</a></i> followed in 1987, <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi_High" title="Degrassi High">Degrassi High</a></i> premiered in 1989, and the television movie <i><a href="/wiki/School%27s_Out_(1992_film)" title="School's Out (1992 film)">School's Out</a></i> aired in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Schuyler and original Degrassi series head writer Yan Moore began developing a new television drama in 1999. As the months progressed, they began to think about what had happened to the characters of <i>Degrassi High</i> to develop a school-reunion theme. However, they decided that a series would not work effectively if based around adults instead of children. Moore realized that the character <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emma_Nelson" title="Emma Nelson">Emma Nelson</a>, born at the end of <i>Degrassi Junior High</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s second season, would soon be entering <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">junior high school</a>, and development for the series took a new direction by focusing on Emma and her school experiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-how_it_all_happened_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-how_it_all_happened-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Schuyler's husband <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stohn" title="Stephen Stohn">Stephen Stohn</a> suggested <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> as the name for the new sequel series, borrowing the concept from <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek:_The_Next_Generation" title="Star Trek: The Next Generation">Star Trek: The Next Generation</a></i>, of which he was a fan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The project was pitched to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CTV_Television" title="CTV Television">CTV</a> in May 2000, with the originally planned reunion episode serving as the pilot to the new series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-how_it_all_happened_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-how_it_all_happened-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_producers.2C_script-writers_and_directors">Executive producers, script-writers and directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Executive producers, script-writers and directors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Produced by Epitome Pictures Inc, in association with CTVglobemedia, renamed <a href="/wiki/Bell_Media" title="Bell Media">Bell Media</a> in 2011, <i>Degrassi</i> receives funding from <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Television_Fund" title="Canadian Television Fund">Canadian Television Fund</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bell_Canada" title="Bell Canada">BCE</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> the Shaw Rocket Fund,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Mountain Cable Program and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Canada" title="Royal Bank of Canada">Royal Bank of Canada</a>, the Bell Broadcast and New Media Fund,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> and the Cogeco Program Development Fund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Linda Schuyler and Stephen Stohn have served as executive producers since the series began. Other Epitome Pictures employees and series crew members have also been credited with the title, including Sara Snow, Brendon Yorke, James Hurst, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aaron_Martin_(producer)" title="Aaron Martin (producer)">Aaron Martin</a>.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crew_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-crew-11">[11]</a></sup> and Sarah Glinski.</p>
<p>Sarah Glinski and Matt Huether are the current story editors, a position previously filled by Shelley Scarrow, James Hurst, Aaron Martin, and Sean Reycraft. Frequent directors include Phil Earnshaw, Stefan Scaini and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bruce_McDonald_(film_director)" title="Bruce McDonald (film director)">Bruce McDonald</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crew_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-crew-11">[11]</a></sup> When production of season three began, a user on the official <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> website with the alias "ExecProducer" began a <a href="/wiki/Internet_forum" title="Internet forum">forum</a> thread titled "Shooting Season 3",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> revealing production details, guest actors, scheduling information and DVD release details. He referred to himself as "Stephen Stohn" in one post, although it was not until the release of <i>Degrassi: Generations - The Official 411</i> in 2005, that Stohn confirmed he was the poster and it was not an imposter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p12_13_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-p12_13-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Episode_format">Episode format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Episode format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="metadata mbox-small" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="Book icon" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="30" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Office-book.svg/30px-Office-book.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Office-book.svg/45px-Office-book.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Office-book.svg/60px-Office-book.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">
<ul style="font-weight: bold">
<li><a href="/wiki/Book:Seasons_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation" title="Book:Seasons of Degrassi: The Next Generation">Book: Seasons of Degrassi: The Next Generation</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Each episode of <i>Degrassi</i> is written following the same formula with two or three storylines (Plot A, Plot B and Plot C). The main storyline, A, opens and closes the episode and is usually driven by a single character. Plot B is usually more comedic in tone and sometimes slightly intertwined with the other stories, often moving <a href="/wiki/Story_arc" title="Story arc">story arcs</a> forward. Plot C was usually used sporadically in a season-long arc, but is now used in every episode as comedic relief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plot_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-plot-14">[14]</a></sup> The problems and issues presented in the episode are not always resolved by the end of the episode, and are carried over to the next, or create a mini-arc over several episodes. The majority of episodes are named after songs from the <a href="/wiki/1980s_in_music" title="1980s in music">1980s</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> and since the <a href="/wiki/Degrassi_(season_10)" title="Degrassi (season 10)">tenth season</a>, episodes are named after songs from the 1990s to the present, representing the entering of a new decade and a completely different cast from the earlier seasons. For the first nine seasons, <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> had been produced as a weekly half-hour <a href="/wiki/Teen_drama" title="Teen drama">teen</a> <a href="/wiki/Comedy-drama" title="Comedy-drama">comedy-drama</a> series, with each season consisting of between fifteen and twenty-four episodes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p12_13_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-p12_13-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to falling viewing figures between seasons six and nine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bailey_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bailey-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jane_Says_P2_figures_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jane_Says_P2_figures-18">[18]</a></sup> the series developed a daily soap opera format for the summer run of the tenth season, and increased the number of episodes to forty-four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-THR-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-20">[20]</a></sup> The tenth season also dropped the tagline "The Next Generation", with only one original cast member remaining, and due to the young audience unfamiliar with the past generation, referring to the series as "Degrassi". Season 13 reverted to airing episodes weekly, but still produced more episodes than prior to the soap opera format, airing a block in the summer of 2013 and also the summer of 2014.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Opening_sequence">Opening sequence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Opening sequence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Degrassi_logo_2013.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="423" data-file-width="1000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Degrassi_logo_2013.png/220px-Degrassi_logo_2013.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Degrassi_logo_2013.png/330px-Degrassi_logo_2013.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Degrassi_logo_2013.png/440px-Degrassi_logo_2013.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Degrassi_logo_2013.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Logo used in seasons 13-14</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i>Degrassi</i> opening sequence follows a two- to three-minute <a href="/wiki/Cold_open" title="Cold open">cold open</a>. During the first five seasons these credits showed the characters on the school premises and followed a mini storyline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Seasons six and seven featured titles with the actors breaking the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_wall" title="Fourth wall">fourth wall</a> and facing the camera, over a montage of character videos from past seasons, saturated with blue colour and gold outlines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The montages behind the characters depicting a major event in that character's storyline. For the eighth season, the show abandoned the style of titles used for the previous two seasons and returned to the original form of showing the characters at school while participating in school-related activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Season thirteen dropped the opening credits, replacing it with an eleven-second montage. This continued into season fourteen. Instead of listing every ensemble actor, after the montage, season thirteen and fourteen episodes credit only the regular actors appearing in that episode.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Theme_music" title="Theme music">theme music</a>, "Whatever It Takes", was composed by Jim McGrath, with lyrics written by Jody Colero and Stephen Stohn. The song include lines such as, "Whatever it takes, I know I can make it through/Be the best, the best I can be", to convey what Colero calls, "a sense of joy and optimism."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411-music_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-411-music-24">[24]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisa_Dalbello" title="Lisa Dalbello">Lisa Dalbello</a> performed the lyrics with a children's choir over an 1980s pop music style tune during the first three seasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411-music_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-411-music-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dave_Ogilvie" title="Dave Ogilvie">Dave Ogilvie</a> and Anthony Valcic of Canadian <a href="/wiki/Industrial_music" title="Industrial music">industrial</a>-pop group <a href="/wiki/Jakalope" title="Jakalope">Jakalope</a> reworked and performed the song with a heavier sound, reflecting the growing maturity of the characters in season four.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411-music_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-411-music-24">[24]</a></sup> For seasons six and seven, the theme—still performed by Jakalope—was remixed and stripped of vocals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-here_comes_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-here_comes-25">[25]</a></sup> A fourth version of the theme song, with lyrics sung by <a href="/wiki/Damhnait_Doyle" title="Damhnait Doyle">Damhnait Doyle</a>, was introduced for the eighth season, and a fifth version of the theme, performed by the in-show band "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_bands#Janie_.26_The_Studs" title="List of Degrassi: The Next Generation bands">Stüdz</a>" is used for the ninth and tenth seasons. For seasons eleven and twelve, a sixth version of the theme song is used, performed by <a href="/wiki/Alexz_Johnson" title="Alexz Johnson">Alexz Johnson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Seasons thirteen and fourteen featured a truncated version of the Alexz Johnson theme.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jim McGrath creates the musical score for each episode using an instrumental version of the theme music. He also works with actors such as <a href="/wiki/Jake_Epstein" title="Jake Epstein">Jake Epstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melissa_McIntyre" title="Melissa McIntyre">Melissa McIntyre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Johnston" title="Jamie Johnston">Jamie Johnston</a>, when writing music for their characters <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Craig_Manning" title="Craig Manning">Craig Manning</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashley_Kerwin" title="Ashley Kerwin">Ashley Kerwin</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Stone_(Degrassi_character)" title="Peter Stone (Degrassi character)">Peter Stone</a> to perform in the bands <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_bands#Downtown_Sasquatch" title="List of Degrassi: The Next Generation bands">Downtown Sasquatch</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_bands#Paige_Michalchuk_and_the_Sexkittens_.28PMS.29" title="List of Degrassi: The Next Generation bands">Paige Michalchuk and the Sexkittens (PMS)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_bands#Hell_Hath_No_Fury" title="List of Degrassi: The Next Generation bands">Hell Hath No Fury</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_bands#Janie_.26_The_Studs" title="List of Degrassi: The Next Generation bands">Stüdz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> In addition to being scored, <i>Degrassi</i> features a mix of original <a href="/wiki/Emo" title="Emo">emo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> and pop music. Popular songs are used sparingly in the series, mainly because of budget constraints. Usually, music supervisor Jody Colero selects songs from little-known, unsigned Canadian artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411-music_24-3"><a href="#cite_note-411-music-24">[24]</a></sup> When these songs are included, they originate from a <a href="/wiki/Diegesis" title="Diegesis">diegetic</a> source. Examples of this can be seen in the first-season episode "Jagged Little Pill", when well-known songs are played during Ashley's house party, at the wedding reception in the fifth-season episode "Weddings, Parties, Anything", and during the party scene in the seventh-season episode "Everything She Wants".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming_locations">Filming locations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Filming locations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Degrassi</i> universe is set on <a href="/wiki/De_Grassi_Street" title="De Grassi Street">De Grassi Street</a> in Toronto, Ontario. The four previous series were filmed on and near the street.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> However, <i>Degrassi</i> is filmed at Epitome Pictures' four soundstages and backlot located at the company's 100,000-square-foot (9,300 m<sup>2</sup>) production studios in Toronto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studios_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-studios-34">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Facade" title="Facade">facade</a> of Degrassi Community School is the exterior of Studio C, and uses the same colours and glass pattern as <a href="/wiki/Centennial_College" title="Centennial College">Centennial College</a>, which was used to depict the school during <i>Degrassi High</i>. The area in front of this facade features a "hoarding area" where students gather, a street, and a bus stop across the road.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studios_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-studios-34">[34]</a></sup> The studio's backlot is used for exterior shots of the characters' houses, which is one unit dressed differently for each house, and The Dot Grill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-backlot_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-backlot-35">[35]</a></sup> The building for The Dot is the only one on the backlot large enough to allow filming inside; scenes taking places inside the school and house interiors are filmed on one of four sound stages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studios_34-2"><a href="#cite_note-studios-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Studio A contains sets for the school's hallways, washrooms, cafeteria and classrooms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studios_34-3"><a href="#cite_note-studios-34">[34]</a></sup> The hallways are stenciled with phrases such as "the perfect human being is all human", which were found at the Etobicoke School for the Arts, one of the many schools that set designers used during their original research. The washroom set has graffiti on the walls to look authentic, and is used for the girls' and boys' room; urinals are installed and removed as needed. The set used for the cafeteria is "purposefully bland to take the edge off the rest of the school looking so beautiful."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stage_a_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-stage_a-36">[36]</a></sup> It is also used as the studio's cafeteria where the cast and crew eat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stage_a_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-stage_a-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to being used as the exterior of the school, Studio C holds sets for the school's entrance foyer, the gymnasium, the media lab and a hallway with lockers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studios_34-4"><a href="#cite_note-studios-34">[34]</a></sup> As the series progressed and the budget increased, a stairway and balcony was installed in the foyer in an attempt to get characters off the floor and not all appear in the same <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plane_(mathematics)" title="Plane (mathematics)">geometric plane</a>. For the first few seasons, the gym floor was made of real wooden floorboards; due to warping, it was replaced by concrete painted to look like wood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stage_c_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-stage_c-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Studio B contains the sets for the characters' houses and <i>The Core</i> newspaper office which was introduced in season six. It also held sets for <i><a href="/wiki/Instant_Star" title="Instant Star">Instant Star</a></i>, another Epitome Pictures production. The fourth studio, Studio D, houses all the production offices, dressing rooms, and make-up and hair departments. The pool hall and university campus club sets were built in Studio D for the seventh season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studios_34-5"><a href="#cite_note-studios-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/York_University" title="York University">York University</a>'s Keele Campus in Toronto served as the location for various sites at Smithdale University.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Episodes">Episodes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Episodes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_roles">Main roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Main roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_characters" title="List of Degrassi: The Next Generation characters">List of Degrassi: The Next Generation characters</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Mother_and_Child_Reunion_(Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation)#Cast" title="Mother and Child Reunion (Degrassi: The Next Generation)">Casting of pilot episode "Mother and Child Reunion"</a></div>
<p>For the new generation of students, producers auditioned over six hundred school-aged children in an attempt to provide characters to which the teenaged target-audience could relate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The decision to cast age-similar actors was purposeful to contrast the series from other shows of the same period such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buffy_the_Vampire_Slayer_(TV_series)" title="Buffy the Vampire Slayer (TV series)">Buffy the Vampire Slayer</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dawson%27s_Creek" title="Dawson's Creek">Dawson's Creek</a></i>, which had cast actors in their twenties as teenagers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-body_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-body-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Eleven children were given star <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billing_(film)" title="Billing (film)">billing</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_1)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 1)">first season</a>. Sarah Barrable-Tishauer portrayed the lonely high-achiever <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberty_Van_Zandt" title="Liberty Van Zandt">Liberty Van Zandt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-body_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-body-40">[40]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Clark_(actor)" title="Daniel Clark (actor)">Daniel Clark</a> played bad-boy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sean_Cameron_(Degrassi_character)" title="Sean Cameron (Degrassi character)">Sean Cameron</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Collins" title="Lauren Collins">Lauren Collins</a> was cast as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paige_Michalchuk" title="Paige Michalchuk">Paige Michalchuk</a>, the school's head cheerleader and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_bee_(subculture)" title="Queen bee (subculture)">queen bee</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Cooley" title="Ryan Cooley">Ryan Cooley</a> portrayed class clown <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J.T._Yorke" title="J.T. Yorke">James Tiberius "J.T." Yorke</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe_2001_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Globe_2001-42">[42]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Jake_Goldsbie" title="Jake Goldsbie">Jake Goldsbie</a> cast as J.T.'s best friend, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toby_Isaacs" title="Toby Isaacs">Toby Isaacs</a>, a computer geek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe_2001_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Globe_2001-42">[42]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)">Aubrey "Drake" Graham</a> portrayed basketball star <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jimmy_Brooks" title="Jimmy Brooks">Jimmy Brooks</a>, who is from a wealthy family. <a href="/wiki/Shane_Kippel" title="Shane Kippel">Shane Kippel</a> played school bully <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gavin_Mason" title="Gavin Mason">Gavin "Spinner" Mason</a>. <a href="/wiki/Miriam_McDonald" title="Miriam McDonald">Miriam McDonald</a> was cast as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emma_Nelson" title="Emma Nelson">Emma Nelson</a>, an environmental rights activist, with <a href="/wiki/Cassie_Steele" title="Cassie Steele">Cassie Steele</a> cast in the role of Emma's best friend, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manny_Santos_(Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation)" title="Manny Santos (Degrassi: The Next Generation)">Manuela "Manny" Santos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe_2001_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-Globe_2001-42">[42]</a></sup> Melissa McIntyre portrayed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashley_Kerwin" title="Ashley Kerwin">Ashley Kerwin</a>, the perfect girl who attracts the popular boys, and who the other girls are jealous of.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Christina Schmidt portrayed the overweight and insecure <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terri_McGreggor" title="Terri McGreggor">Terri McGreggor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Providing ties to the previous series in the <i>Degrassi</i> universe, <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Brogren" title="Stefan Brogren">Stefan Brogren</a> was approached to play his old character <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archie_%22Snake%22_Simpson" title='Archie "Snake" Simpson'>Archie "Snake" Simpson</a>, now working at the school as the <a href="/wiki/Media_studies" title="Media studies">media immersion</a> teacher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Dan Woods reprised his role as English teacher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mr._Raditch" title="Mr. Raditch">Mr. Raditch</a>, now promoted to school principal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pat_Mastroianni" title="Pat Mastroianni">Pat Mastroianni</a> returned to his role as <a href="/wiki/Joey_Jeremiah" title="Joey Jeremiah">Joey Jeremiah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Stepto" title="Amanda Stepto">Amanda Stepto</a> also returned to the franchise to play her character <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christine_Nelson" title="Christine Nelson">Christine "Spike" Nelson</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Recurring_character" title="Recurring character">recurring role</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sopranos_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sopranos-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the pilot episode, former <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi_Junior_High" title="Degrassi Junior High">Degrassi Junior High</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi_High" title="Degrassi High">Degrassi High</a></i> actors Danah Jean Brown (Trish Skye), <a href="/wiki/Darrin_Brown" title="Darrin Brown">Darrin Brown</a> (Dwayne Myers), Michael Carry (Simon Dexter), Irene Courakos (Alexa Pappadopoulos), Chrissa Erodotou (Diana Economopoulos), <a href="/wiki/Anais_Granofsky" title="Anais Granofsky">Anais Granofsky</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lucy_Fernandez" title="Lucy Fernandez">Lucy Fernandez</a>), Rebecca Haines (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kathleen_Mead" title="Kathleen Mead">Kathleen Mead</a>), Sarah Holmes (Alison Hunter), <a href="/wiki/Neil_Hope" title="Neil Hope">Neil Hope</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Derek_Wheeler" title="Derek Wheeler">Derek "Wheels" Wheeler</a>), Kyra Levy (Maya Goldberg), Cathy Keenan (Liz O'Rourke), <a href="/wiki/Stacie_Mistysyn" title="Stacie Mistysyn">Stacie Mistysyn</a> (<a href="/wiki/Caitlin_Ryan_(Degrassi)" title="Caitlin Ryan (Degrassi)">Caitlin Ryan</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Siluck_Saysanasy" title="Siluck Saysanasy">Siluck Saysanasy</a> (Yick Yu) reprised their roles for the class reunion storyline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-s1e1_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-s1e1-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_2)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 2)">season two</a>, Mastroianni returned to the <i>Degrassi</i> franchise in a starring role as Joey Jeremiah, a car salesman and single father of two children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Joey's stepson, musician <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Craig_Manning" title="Craig Manning">Craig Manning</a>, played by <a href="/wiki/Jake_Epstein" title="Jake Epstein">Jake Epstein</a>, is a new student at Degrassi Community School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Three other new characters were introduced in season two in recurring roles. <a href="/wiki/Stacey_Farber" title="Stacey Farber">Stacey Farber</a> played <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ellie_Nash" title="Ellie Nash">Ellie Nash</a>, a goth whose home life is in turmoil,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ellis_2005_64.E2.80.9365_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis_2005_64.E2.80.9365-56">[56]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Adamo_Ruggiero" title="Adamo Ruggiero">Adamo Ruggiero</a> portrayed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marco_Del_Rossi" title="Marco Del Rossi">Marco Del Rossi</a>, who is struggling to accept the reality that he is homosexual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melissa_Di_Marco" title="Melissa Di Marco">Melissa Di Marco</a> was cast as science and gym teacher <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daphne_Hatzilakos" title="Daphne Hatzilakos">Daphne Hatzilakos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> Mistysyn also returned to her former <i>Degrassi</i> role as Joey's ex-high school sweetheart, Caitlyn Ryan, who in the years following graduation has become a world-renowned journalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ellis_2005_64.E2.80.9365_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ellis_2005_64.E2.80.9365-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_3)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 3)">season three</a>, Farber, Ruggiero and Mistysyn were given regular roles, as were <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Lewis" title="Andrea Lewis">Andrea Lewis</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hazel_Aden" title="Hazel Aden">Hazel Aden</a>) and Stepto, who had held recurring roles since the first season. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Lobel" title="Mike Lobel">Mike Lobel</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay_Hogart" title="Jay Hogart">Jay Hogart</a>), Deanna Casaluce (Alex Nuñez), <a href="/wiki/Ephraim_Ellis" title="Ephraim Ellis">Ephraim Ellis</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rick_Murray" title="Rick Murray">Rick Murray</a>) and <a href="/wiki/John_Bregar" title="John Bregar">John Bregar</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dylan_Michalchuk" title="Dylan Michalchuk">Dylan Michalchuk</a>) were introduced in recurring roles as new students. Towards the end of the season, Schmidt's character, Terri McGreggor, was written out of the show when her possessive boyfriend Rick pushed her to the ground and knocked her head against a rock, causing her to fall into a coma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="766" data-file-width="1141" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg/200px-ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg/300px-ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg/400px-ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ETalk2008-Degrassi_Cast.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Some of the cast of <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_8)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 8)">season eight</a> make an appearance at the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ETalk" title="ETalk">eTalk</a></i> Festival Party during the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">Toronto International Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Over the course of the ten seasons of <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i>, there have been several departures from the series. <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_6)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 6)">Season six</a> depicted the first death of one of the show's main characters when J.T. Yorke was stabbed and killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Clark's character Sean Cameron has been written out of the show twice. He left the series during the fourth season in the wake of the death of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rick_Murray" title="Rick Murray">Rick Murray</a>, and returned for the sixth season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> but departed the series again at the end of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> At the end of <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_5)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 5)">season five</a> several main characters graduated from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Degrassi_Community_School" title="Degrassi Community School">Degrassi Community School</a>, and either left the series or went on to university.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-here_comes_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-here_comes-25">[25]</a></sup> Six new characters were introduced in <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_7)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 7)">season seven</a> in a storyline where nearby rival high school Lakehurst merged with Degrassi following a fire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_8)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 8)">Season eight</a> saw many changes when many of the existing cast members, including Collins, Farber, Graham, Stepto, Ruggiero, and DiMarco either moved to recurring status or left the series entirely. The exodus of several major cast members was reportedly an executive decision that left the actors and producers on bad terms, with Graham stating in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> that "[the producers] did us foul."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VIBE.com_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-VIBE.com-65">[65]</a></sup> Thirteen actors were added to the main cast to replace them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-September_press_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-September_press-66">[66]</a></sup> By <a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_(season_9)" title="Degrassi: The Next Generation (season 9)">season nine</a>, Brogren, McDonald, Steele and Kippel were the only actors from season one who remained in the series as storylines began to focus on a new generation of children attending the school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Enrols_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Enrols-67">[67]</a></sup> This was done to avoid moving the show to a primarily college setting, as the first generation cast aged or "graduated" out of Degrassi Community School into college.</p>
<p>As of season 10, none of the characters from the earlier seasons remain, with the exception of Brogren, whose character has been promoted to the principal of Degrassi Community School; the series now centres on the new generation of Degrassi students.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guest_roles">Guest roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Guest roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Besides Brogren, Mistysyn, Stepto, and Mastroianni having starring roles, other actors from <i>Degrassi Junior High</i> and <i>Degrassi High</i> have returned to guest star in their old roles throughout <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i>'s run. As well as the pilot episode featuring the return of many Degrassi alumni,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-s1e1_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-s1e1-52">[52]</a></sup> Granofsky made a second guest appearance during the second season in the episode "White Wedding" when her character attends the wedding of Spike and Snake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> In a fifth-season episode, Keenan and Hope guest star when their characters return to console Spike and Snake after their marriage breaks down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Movie director <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Smith" title="Kevin Smith">Kevin Smith</a> has been a fan of the Degrassi series from the early 1990s, when he worked at a convenience store in Leonardo, New Jersey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quickstop_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-quickstop-71">[71]</a></sup> Actor <a href="/wiki/Jason_Mewes" title="Jason Mewes">Jason Mewes</a> was his co-worker at the store and also became a fan. Every Sunday morning at work, Smith and Mewes watched episodes of <i>Degrassi Junior High</i> and <i>Degrassi High</i> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">Public Broadcasting Service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viewaskew_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-viewaskew-72">[72]</a></sup> Smith enjoyed the earlier series and has acknowledged an infatuation with Stacie Mistysyn. He has also paid homage to <i>Degrassi</i> by referring to it in several of his films. He named a <i><a href="/wiki/Clerks" title="Clerks">Clerks</a></i> character <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caitlin_Bree" title="Caitlin Bree">Caitlin Bree</a> after Mistysin's <i>Degrassi</i> character, Caitlin Ryan,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viewaskew_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-viewaskew-72">[72]</a></sup> wrote <a href="/wiki/Shannen_Doherty" title="Shannen Doherty">Shannen Doherty</a>'s character Rene wearing a <i>Degrassi</i> jacket throughout his <i><a href="/wiki/Mallrats" title="Mallrats">Mallrats</a></i> film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> and had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jason_Lee_(entertainer)" title="Jason Lee (entertainer)">Jason Lee</a>'s character in <i><a href="/wiki/Chasing_Amy" title="Chasing Amy">Chasing Amy</a></i> specifically mention <i>Degrassi Junior High</i> as a TV show he wants to watch, rather than going out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Smith and Mewes guest starred as themselves in the final three episodes of the fourth season. The plot for these episodes involves the pair working on <i>Jay and Silent Bob Go Canadian, Eh!</i>, a fictional feature film in the <a href="/wiki/View_Askewniverse" title="View Askewniverse">View Askewniverse</a>, using Degrassi Community School as a filming location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Singer <a href="/wiki/Alanis_Morissette" title="Alanis Morissette">Alanis Morissette</a>, who had worked with Smith, also guest stars in "Going Down the Road Part One" as herself, acting as the school principal in Smith's film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Smith and Mewes return to <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> as themselves for two episodes in season five. The storyline in the episodes was of the premiere of <i>Jay and Silent Bob Go Canadian, Eh!</i> Alanis Morissette made a cameo appearance as the school principal when scenes from the film were shown during its premiere screening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Smith and Mewes guest starred a third time for four episodes in season eight when many of the characters travelled to Hollywood, Los Angeles. In the episodes, Mewes is the writer-director and protagonist of <i>Mewesical High</i>, which stars a number of Degrassi Community School students. Smith appears in the episodes to support Mewes as he makes his directorial debut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quickstop_71-1"><a href="#cite_note-quickstop-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other actors to appear in <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> include <a href="/wiki/Jayne_Eastwood" title="Jayne Eastwood">Jayne Eastwood</a> as Sean Cameron's mother,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p93_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-p93-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Billy_Ray_Cyrus" title="Billy Ray Cyrus">Billy Ray Cyrus</a> as Duke, a limousine driver who gets arrested, the result of which leaves Jimmy, Hazel, Paige, and Spinner stranded in the street.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p93_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-p93-80">[80]</a></sup> Season seven featured appearances from <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Douglas" title="Shirley Douglas">Shirley Douglas</a> as a university professor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shirley_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-shirley-82">[82]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_The_Children" title="Free The Children">Free The Children</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Craig_Kielburger" title="Craig Kielburger">Craig Kielburger</a>, and English pop singer <a href="/wiki/Natasha_Bedingfield" title="Natasha Bedingfield">Natasha Bedingfield</a> as themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Torrens" title="Jonathan Torrens">Jonathan Torrens</a> guest starred as Emma's father, Shane, in the two-part season three premiere. The character had been played by Bill Parrott in the original series, but he decided not to return the former role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p93_80-2"><a href="#cite_note-p93-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> In season 10, ballroom dancer <a href="/wiki/Jean-Marc_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9reux" title="Jean-Marc Généreux">Jean-Marc Généreux</a> appears as a teacher, in the episodes Adam's transgender secret is revealed. After moving to MuchMusic cameos became more frequent, including <a href="/wiki/Keke_Palmer" title="Keke Palmer">Keke Palmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ben_Mulroney" title="Ben Mulroney">Ben Mulroney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaz_Bono" title="Chaz Bono">Chaz Bono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedley_(band)" title="Hedley (band)">Hedley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fefe_Dobson" title="Fefe Dobson">Fefe Dobson</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcast_and_distribution">Broadcast and distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Broadcast and distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_run_broadcast">First run broadcast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: First run broadcast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation_episodes" title="List of Degrassi: The Next Generation episodes">List of Degrassi: The Next Generation episodes</a></div>
<p>While the earlier Degrassi series aired in Canada on <a href="/wiki/CBC_Television" title="CBC Television">CBC</a>, <i>Degrassi</i> is broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Bell_Media" title="Bell Media">Bell Media</a>-owned stations. Until mid-season nine, it aired on the <a href="/wiki/CTV_Television_Network" title="CTV Television Network">CTV Television Network</a>, but due to a decline in viewing figures since season seven,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bailey_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bailey-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jane_Says_P2_figures_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jane_Says_P2_figures-18">[18]</a></sup> it moved to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_channel" title="Sister channel">sister channel</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MuchMusic" title="MuchMusic">MuchMusic</a> in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-THR_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-THR-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Globe_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Globe-20">[20]</a></sup> In 2013, following a revamp of MuchMusic's schedule,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> the show moved to the Canadian version of <a href="/wiki/MTV_(Canada)" title="MTV (Canada)">MTV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, where the earlier Degrassi series aired on PBS, <i>Degrassi</i> aired on <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cable_network" title="Cable network">cable network</a> <a href="/wiki/TeenNick" title="TeenNick">TeenNick</a> (previously The N), and is the longest-running program on the channel, having aired since the channel's launch in 2002. Seasons six and seven premiered on The N before they aired on CTV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sept_29_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sept_29-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-s6_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-s6-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2015, both MTV Canada and TeenNick announced that they would not renew the show. On June 9, 2015, Epitome Pictures announced that a sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/Degrassi:_Next_Class" title="Degrassi: Next Class">Degrassi: Next Class</a></i>, would premiere on <a href="/wiki/Family_Channel" title="Family Channel">Family Channel</a>, a pay channel owned by DHX Media, in January 2016. In the United States (and internationally), first-run episodes will move to <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix</a>. Episodes will become available on Netflix in Canada following the conclusion of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gandm-dhxepitome_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-gandm-dhxepitome-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbc-degrassifamily_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-degrassifamily-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC1" title="ABC1">ABC1</a> screened the first three seasons in 2002 in its "ABC Kids" line-up and after that the storylines were considered to adult for the late afternoon timeslot. The entire series was aired on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC3" title="ABC3">ABC3</a> in 2010 in a primetime slot, also broadcast on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_(Australia)" title="Nickelodeon (Australia)">Nickelodeon</a> then later <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Australia" title="MTV Australia">MTV</a>.</p>
<p>In South Africa degrassi is set to air in October 2016 on SABC 1.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-broadcast_distribution">Post-broadcast distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Post-broadcast distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Canada, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stripping_(television)" title="Stripping (television)">strip repeats</a> of <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> have aired on <a href="/wiki/CTV_Two" title="CTV Two">CTV Two</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV2_(Canada)" title="MTV2 (Canada)">MTV2</a>, which are owned by Bell Media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In the United States, independent distributor Program Partners and <a href="/wiki/Sony_Pictures_Television" title="Sony Pictures Television">Sony Pictures Television</a>, announced on September 24, 2006 that they acquired the syndication rights to the first 119 episodes of the show in the United States, and any subsequent new episodes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Broadcasting_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Broadcasting-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2006, Program Partners had reached agreements with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tribune_Company" title="Tribune Company">Tribune Company</a> for every station it owned, <a href="/wiki/The_CW_Plus" title="The CW Plus">The CW Plus</a> affiliated stations, and many other stations owned by major <a href="/wiki/Media_conglomerate" title="Media conglomerate">media conglomerates</a>. <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> was cleared in 60% of the country including all five of the top five <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">media markets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> By March 2007, Program Partners had cleared it in over 70% of the country after stations owned by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hearst-Argyle_Television" title="Hearst-Argyle Television">Hearst-Argyle Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Broadcasting_Company" title="Capitol Broadcasting Company">Capitol Broadcasting Company</a>, and <a href="/wiki/ACME_Communications" title="ACME Communications">ACME Communications</a> purchased the syndication.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The series meets the American <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">FCC</a>'s <a href="/wiki/E/I" title="E/I">educational and informational guidelines</a> towards children's programming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-renewed_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-renewed-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="DVD_and_other_new_media_releases">DVD and other new media releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Degrassi:_The_Next_Generation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: DVD and other new media releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first twelve seasons of <i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> have been released on DVD. The box sets are released in Canada by <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Films" title="Alliance Films">Alliance Home Entertainment</a>. In the United States, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FUNimation_Entertainment" title="FUNimation Entertainment">FUNimation Entertainment</a> released the first six seasons and Echo Bridge Entertainment released seasons seven through twelve. Each season boxset includes extra features such as pictures, <a href="/wiki/Karaoke" title="Karaoke">karaoke</a> sessions, audition tapes, <a href="/wiki/Blooper" title="Blooper">bloopers</a>, deleted scenes and more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In Australia, seasons 1 to 4 were released by <a href="/wiki/Umbrella_Entertainment" title="Umbrella Entertainment">Umbrella Entertainment</a> in 2010 and 2011. These DVDs are compatible with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Region_4" title="Region 4">region 4</a> code,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Umbrella_Entertainment_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-Umbrella_Entertainment-99">[99]</a></sup> which is in use in Australia, New Zealand, Oceania, Mexico, and Central and South America.</p>
<p>The three-episode story arc from the fourth season in which Kevin Smith and Jason Mewes guest star has also been released as a single disc Region 1 DVD. FUNimation Entertainment released the disc on November 8, 2005, in two versions: the first subtitled as "Uncut, Uncensored and Unrated",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.26SBU_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-J.26SBU-100">[100]</a></sup> and the second, "Rated."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.26SBR_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-J.26SBR-101">[101]</a></sup> Each release has the same DVD extras, including an interview with Kevin Smith, bloopers and a <i>Jay and Silent Bob</i> Photo Album, except the Unrated release also features episode commentaries by Kevin Smith, Jason Mewes, Stacie Mistysyn, the associate producer Jim Jackman and writer Aaron Martin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J.26SBU_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-J.26SBU-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Degrassi: The Next Generation</i> is also available in various <a href="/wiki/New_media" title="New media">new media</a> formats. Episodes are <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streamed</a> on the websites of MuchMusic and TeenNick to viewers with Canadian or US <a href="/wiki/IP_address" title="IP address">IP addresses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Registered users of the Canadian and American <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Stores</a> can purchase episodes for playback on home computers and certain <a href="/wiki/IPod" title="IPod">iPods</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In Canada, <a href="/wiki/Puretracks" title="Puretracks">Puretracks</a> also offers episodes for download. They are issued as a <a href="/wiki/Windows_Media" title="Windows Media">Windows Media</a> 10 file, and the purchaser owns them forever, although the episodes can only be burned onto a disc three times and copied to a device three times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Puretracks_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-Puretracks-105">[105]</a></sup> In the US, <a href="/wiki/Zune" title="Zune">Zune</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xbox_Live_Marketplace" title="Xbox Live Marketplace">Xbox Live Marketplace</a> sell every episode of the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of July 2016, the first two seasons were uploaded to YouTube on the official Degrassi channel, and are free to view.</p>
